### Post by K.Mandla on 2008-07-31
**Rules:**
[INDENT][LIST=1]
[*]Forum guidelines on content apply. In other words, safe for kids and safe for work.

[*]Try not to quote embedded images; take a moment to snip them out.

[*]Off-topic posts will be edited or moved.

[*]Thumbnail your image, or use the forum's attachment system. Full-size embedded images are annoying and will be snipped mercilessly.

[*]Take a moment and tell everyone the details of your desktop, such as the theme name, the wallpaper name, the icons and any programs you're using in the image.
[/LIST][/INDENT]
Enjoy!

### Post by Arathorn on 2008-07-31
Since I posted my desktop in the previous thread just two hours ago, I take the liberty of reposting it here.

It's KDE 4.1 with the Arezzo plasma theme and the Oxygen window decoration (without the ugly stripes) and icons.
The wallpaper is from [Florian Freundt]("http://florian.freundt.org/W_Vector.html") (I have three of them to rotate every five minutes) and I use [Legendum]("http://home.kabelfoon.nl/%7Eslam/fonts/fonts.html") as system font. All in all pretty straightforward but the idea is to look beautiful without distracting me from my work.

### Post by klange on 2008-07-31
Not quite August yet for me, but I guess I'll get a head start by reposting my last entry to the July thread:

[[img]http://random.ogunderground.com/workstation/anytime/thumbs/human_dark_murrina.png[/img]](http://random.ogunderground.com/workstation/anytime/human_dark_murrina.png) [[img]http://random.ogunderground.com/workstation/anytime/thumbs/human_dark_murrina2.png[/img]](http://random.ogunderground.com/workstation/anytime/human_dark_murrina2.png)

Normally I'd be running Cairo-Dock, but I stick to the newest SVN revision which is currently broken such that it seg faults soon after starting. Theme is another variation of my Fusion-Live Dark Murrina, set up for a more Human orange than my ITT one. Despite being on Intrepid, the wallpaper is of course the background-only Hardy wall.

I completely missed the update in Intrepid that gave us tabbed Nautilus and only noticed it because I accidentally hit Ctrl+T when moving my screenshots around.

I've gone back to having Nautilus render my desktop on my laptop so I could set up all three of my machines in the same way.

### Post by Browncoatdevil on 2008-07-31
Hellow:

I wish I could say that I figured it out, but here's where I got it:

[http://icehot.wordpress.com/2008/05/11/ubuntu-hardy-tutorial-embed-terminal-into-your-desktop/](http://icehot.wordpress.com/2008/05/11/ubuntu-hardy-tutorial-embed-terminal-into-your-desktop/)

To make it work the way I wanted, all I had to do was change the x and y positions and leave out the non-movable/non-resizable window rules.

### Post by dbbolton on 2008-08-01
> **Truedream said:**
> I changed the *gnome-fs-directory.png* in Eikon directory with the one from *Crashbit/places/192x192* folder. But still no go. Am I missing something or doing something wrong?

Try the most current version of the theme (link provided above). Also, use the 128x128 icon, since that's the size of the other Eikon icons.

> **pt123 said:**
> In the file manager how did you get the "desktop" folder to be replaced by an icon? I didn't think this was possible in Gnome.

Again, that isn't Gnome. It's Xfce, and the file manager is Thunar, not Nautilus. However, I think you can make a custom desktop icon in Gnome (on Hardy) like so:

Save this code as ~/Desktop/.directory

```

[Desktop Entry]
Encoding=UTF-8
Type=Directory
BgImage=
Icon=desktop
Name=Desktop

```

### Post by ayoli on 2008-08-01
> **Yes said:**
> Very nice.  May I see your .screenrc?

Sure,
```
#change the hardstatus settings
hardstatus alwayslastline
hardstatus string '%{= kG}[ %{G}%H %{g}][%= %{= kw}%?%-Lw%?%{r}(%{W}%n*%f%t%?(%u)%?%{r})%{w}%?%+Lw%?%?%= %{g}][%{B} %d/%m %{W}%c %{g}]'
#scrollback
termcapinfo xterm ti@:te@

```

### Post by dbbolton on 2008-08-01
> **pt123 said:**
> Thanks but didn't work out with Gnome it created an Icon in Desktop folder called "Desktop" which can be seen only when see "hidden" files is turned on.
Another thing you can try is to right-click on the desktop icon in nautilus, choose properties, then click on the folder icon in the dialogue box. This should let you choose a custom icon (although it will still carry the desktop emblem).

### Post by SunnyRabbiera on 2008-08-02
> **jcway212 said:**
> Ok, total newb question...How do I install this theme...I dont want the wallpaper, but I love the theme. I have emerald theme manager, but it says that the download did not have a theme package or something like that.

Thanks for the help

go to the link he posted here:
[http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Elegant-Blue?content=85622](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Elegant-Blue?content=85622)
then once it downloads extract it where you downloaded it to
go inside the folder and right click either folder and select "create archive" (make sure to do this to both of them)
after that go to your desktop and right click it and select "change desktop background"
go to the "theme" tab
click the "install" button
and go to where you have your files and install the tars.
simple.

---

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-08-02
[[IMG]http://c.imagehost.org/t/0662/faithscreen.jpg[/IMG]](http://c.imagehost.org/view/0662/faithscreen.png) [[IMG]http://c.imagehost.org/t/0893/faithscreen2.jpg[/IMG]](http://c.imagehost.org/view/0893/faithscreen2.png)

Wordle is indeed a great website.

I inserted the text of Unitarian Universalism's seven Principles, UU's six Sources and also part of the text explaining the history of the Flaming Chalice symbol, picked a colour scheme and clapped my hands with joy when I saw Coolvetica was available. Then I just added the Chalice to the screenshots of the word clouds I got (to give the impression the words and principles expressed emanate from the flame), and voilà, a wallpaper to go with these days of quiet reflection after Knoxville's shootings. I did the same to create the banner of a blog I'm planning to open.

Also in the pics, the theme Glow Water, with the usual Eikon icons, Calibri bold 8 (Helvetica 9 on my Conky) and once again the Chalice at my Xfce menu.

Oh, and by the way, don't even try to go to Wordle using the IcedTea version of Java. I nearly lost my mind before I found out it only works with Sun's official version. At least in my PC it does.

### Post by dbbolton on 2008-08-02
> **crhylove said:**
> Looks like gnome, but I agree, this one is awesome.  How do we make this the default Ubuntu desktop?
For the third time, it's Xfce. Actually, it's not even Ubuntu. It's Debian (cf. menu icon).

People have been complaining about the default Ubuntu artwork for years. Personally, I like it because I think it's distinct. It's not gray and blue like nearly every other distro (Debian, Fedora, PCLinuxOS, Mandriva, Dreamlinux, etc.). However, the Blubuntu project seeks to "alleviate" this.

### Post by Koori23 on 2008-08-02
> **cardinals_fan said:**

Thank ya..

I wonder if anyone notices the fundamental ideology that's defined in my themes.. 

I despise clutter (my definition anyway). 

I'm very particular about color matching wallpapers to window borders or the GTK colors or whatever. 

None of my wallpapers have actual graphics on them.. They are very simple backdrops.

I don't understand the value of Conky, Icons on the desktop (I use XFCE, if I want it, it's on my right click menu.)

That's what's beautiful about this window managers, you can pretty much change them to whatever you want.. It's great.

### Post by crhylove on 2008-08-03
Most of my clients are corporate users, teachers, people who need MS Office badly until they realize that Open Office is just as good, but are afraid of change.  For them, the setup I just showed provides LOTS of wow, and all for free, and with better included apps:

Firefox
Transmission
Pidgin
Open Office
Gimp
Rhythmbox
VLC

I've made more WOW kind of designs, but many conservative computer users (primarily in offices) can actually become frightened by too radical designs.  Most of them are frightened by default Ubuntu, and not just because of the brown (though they universally dislike that as well), but because there are two panels (WHAT DO I DO!?!?).

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2008-08-03
> **crhylove said:**
> Most of my clients are corporate users, teachers, people who need MS Office badly until they realize that Open Office is just as good, but are afraid of change.  For them, the setup I just showed provides LOTS of wow, and all for free, and with better included apps:

Firefox
Transmission
Pidgin
Open Office
Gimp
Rhythmbox
VLC

I've made more WOW kind of designs, but many conservative computer users (primarily in offices) can actually become frightened by too radical designs.  Most of them are frightened by default Ubuntu, and not just because of the brown (though they universally dislike that as well), but because there are two panels (WHAT DO I DO!?!?). I concur with this. For someone who is enthusiastic about computers, 'bling' will capture their attention. However, for the majority of people who'd sooner they didn't have to use a computer at all, obviousness; simplicity; readability and familiarity are key to making their user experience as pain-free as possible.

> **Sealbhach said:**
> Dude, she's a drawing. :confused:


.She's the representation of the young, sexually mature human form with nice proportions; symmetry and a smooth texture. Unrealistic and surreal as it may be, more than 100,000 years of mammalian/ape/human evolution is telling me to mate with it and spread my seed because my offspring would be the genetically better for it.

Alternatively, 20 years of flawed upbringing is telling me to resent and be suspicious of it.

### Post by cicatriz on 2008-08-04
This is my lightly-customized Gnome desktop from Intrepid, using the Darklooks theme, whose default availability I am not sure of.

As a side note, I don't mean to deride any of the beautiful desktop setups posted here, but does anyone else find that each and every subpixel-antialiased font (maybe with the exception of the one with Myriad Pro, which is rather pricey) sucks out loud?  I am using MgOpen Cosmetica for mostly everything, but I cannot stand seeing the lack of contrast and sharpness it or any other font used here presents.  To my eyes it's like the whole screen has been rendered with a JPEG quality setting of around 75, particularly on dark backgrounds.

Is there a happy compromise between aliasing and antialiasing?  Fonts with Ubuntu have so many variables (hinting, Autohinter/Native, BCI/non-BCI) yet I can't produce something that is clear and has proper kerning. Windows' ClearType is awful, and OS X looks too bold and still shows a lot of artifacts around edges; maybe I'm just not cut out for this blurry font business?  :)

---

### Post by dbbolton on 2008-08-04
> **markp1989 said:**
> tried it with out the panel, but i didnt like it, any light panels you would recomend?

i would like a menu,window switcher and a notification area, anything else doesnt matter
Personally, I think pypanel makes a great Openbox companion. It's in the Ubuntu repos.

For the menu, see this article: [http://crunchbang.org/archives/2008/03/14/invoke-openboxs-menu-with-xdotool/](http://crunchbang.org/archives/2008/03/14/invoke-openboxs-menu-with-xdotool/)

Then you can make a pypanel launcher whose command will launch the Openbox menu :D

### Post by andrek on 2008-08-05
> **cardinals_fan said:**
> I love Arch too ;)

Would you mind sharing your tint and trayer configs?

Tint - [http://pastebin.com/f22b2ce4d](http://pastebin.com/f22b2ce4d) (You need Neutra Text and Myriad Pro fonts - get them or replace them in config file - /home/user/.config/tint/tintrc)
Trayer - ```
trayer --edge bottom --align right --widthtype request --height 18 --expand false --transparent true --alpha 255 --margin 8 --distance 11
```
( open trayer using above command using ALT + F2 window, terminal, whatever )

---

### Post by dbbolton on 2008-08-06
> **What is in a name? said:**
> 
Trying to figure out why my Nautilus bookmarks appear in a submenu under the Places menu instead of directly appearing in a list as they used to in the past.

I think it is automated based on how many bookmarks you have. For instance, if you only have a few, they appear as a list, but if you have several, they appear in a submenu.

---

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-08-06
> **dbbolton said:**
> I think it is automated based on how many bookmarks you have. For instance, if you only have a few, they appear as a list, but if you have several, they appear in a submenu.

Geez, you're right! I reduced my bookmarks to a number of 5, and now they appear in a list. Thanks!!!

---

### Post by dbbolton on 2008-08-06
> **What is in a name? said:**
> Geez, you're right! I reduced my bookmarks to a number of 5, and now they appear in a list. Thanks!!!

### Post by dbbolton on 2008-08-06
> **What is in a name? said:**
> [[IMG]http://c.imagehost.org/t/0277/orange.jpg[/IMG]]("http://c.imagehost.org/view/0277/orange.png") [[IMG]http://c.imagehost.org/t/0069/orange2.jpg[/IMG]]("http://c.imagehost.org/view/0069/orange2.png")

Pretty much the same as my previous screenshots, except that now I'm using Glow Lava (today's update), and the Blended Small Metacity theme, until there is a closer companion to the Glow suite.

EDIT: As usual, icon issues under GNOME. How can you change the horizontal space between the icons in Nautilus? Is it even possible?
There's an option called "Compact layout" in the preferences. It will put them very close together. Other than that, you might be able to change the default zoom level. Not sure if that will affect the spacing.

BTW, What is that icon theme again?

### Post by perfectska04@hotmail.com on 2008-08-07
> **dbbolton said:**
> Is it just me, or does the Gnome Colors start-here logo look an awful lot like the Windows logo?

A few people have told me that, but If there is any similarity, it's not intentional. They are just simple cubes representing the available colors. They're necessary because not everyone uses Ubuntu, and the default GNOME foot looks quite awful in dark themes. 

Worst case scenario, Ubuntu users can just delete the icon and the default Ubuntu logo will show up.

### Post by perfectska04@hotmail.com on 2008-08-07
> **What is in a name? said:**
> Just a question...
How in the world can one have flat buttons on GNOME-panel's taskbar?

If using clearlooks, you can make them flatter by changing the reliefstyle of the panel to 0.

With murrine you could try playing with the hilight ratio... And I think if you use a pixmap bg (right clicking the panel) the inactive buttons dissapear.

---

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-08-07
> **perfectska04@hotmail.com said:**
> If using clearlooks, you can make them flatter by changing the reliefstyle of the panel to 0.

With murrine you could try playing with the hilight ratio... And I think if you use a pixmap bg (right clicking the panel) the inactive buttons dissapear.

Hey, thanks!

I tried the latter suggestion, and it worked just fine. I really wanted the inactive buttons to disappear (something you can get easily done in Xfce), but it was bothering me in GNOME. Awesome!

And by the way, I love your themes. Besides their pleasant look, they also teach a lot.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2008-08-08
> **Perpetual said:**
> How did you make your gnome-menu black?  Thanks!

My whole system theme is quite dark but for selective colouring:

```
class "GtkMenu"        style "theme-menu"
class "GtkMenuItem"    style "theme-menu-item"

style "theme-menu" # = "theme-default" # optionally inherits base style
{
	fg[NORMAL] = "#ffffff"
	bg[NORMAL] = "#000000"
}

style "theme-menu-item"
{
	fg[PRELIGHT] = "#ffffff"
	bg[SELECTED] = "#707070"
}
```

As for my question, looks as if I've got my answer; tear-offs have to be implemented in the individual GTK+ apps. So much for a universal style setting.


Now for new questions. 

Firstly, how do you get rid of these in the Murrine engine?

[img]http://img225.imageshack.us/img225/4481/cropqy2.png[/img]

Secondly, if I've defined a separate style for GTKButton and my base theme bg[NORMAL/bg[ACTIVE] settings are being overridden by my button sub-style (as they're supposed to be), why aren't my base theme's fg[ACTIVE]/fg[NORMAL] settings being overridden by the new sub-style in the same manner?

eg.

```
style "theme-button" = "theme-default"
{
	fg[ACTIVE]		= "#ffffff" # -not working
	fg[NORMAL]		= "#ffffff" # -not working
	bg[NORMAL]		= "#252525" # -working
	bg[ACTIVE]		= "#707070" # -working
	bg[PRELIGHT]		= "#333333" # -working
}
```

Are button labels a separate class which have to be defined individually?


Here's my full desktop. I've been trying to perfect my GTK theme, making it as small-screen as possible without losing usability:

[[IMG]http://img108.imageshack.us/img108/1194/screenes9.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img108.imageshack.us/my.php?image=screenes9.jpg)

---

Secondly, if I've defined a separate style for GTKButton and my base theme bg[NORMAL/bg[ACTIVE] settings are being overridden by my button sub-style (as they're supposed to be), why aren't my base theme's fg[ACTIVE]/fg[NORMAL] settings being overridden by the new sub-style in the same manner?

style "theme-button" = "theme-default"
{
	fg[ACTIVE]		= "#ffffff" # -not working
	fg[NORMAL]		= "#ffffff" # -not working
	bg[NORMAL]		= "#252525" # -working

About the Murrina question, set this in your engine options:

```

menustyle         = 0

```

### Post by K.Mandla on 2008-08-08
Just to be snarky, this is Crux Linux pretending to be an Intrepid Ibex mockup. :p

[[img]http://xs130.xs.to/xs130/08325/screenshot-2008-08-08-154124-608.jpg.xs.jpg[/img]](http://xs.to/xs.php?h=xs130&d=08325&f=screenshot-2008-08-08-154124-608.jpg)

That's the [NodokaOrangeBlack theme]("http://box-look.org/content/show.php/NodokaOrangeBlack?content=85035") for Openbox sporting the [Crashbit icons]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/CrashBit?content=71140") with the Google [Droid font]("http://benno.id.au/blog/2007/11/14/android-filesystems") everywhere.

The GTK2 style is a hacked-apart version of NewHuman that comes straight from the [current Intrepid archives]("http://packages.ubuntu.com/intrepid/human-theme"), realigned to use the [Rezlooks engine]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Rezlooks+GTK+Engine?content=39179").

Wallpaper also comes from the [Intrepid archives]("http://packages.ubuntu.com/intrepid/ubuntu-wallpapers"). That's the Heron Simple image, if I remember right.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2008-08-09
Okay, got question.

Lets say I want to have system stats (CPU usage; memory usage; disk usage) along the very top of my screen. I don't want it to appear above other windows, nor do I want it to take up anymore than 12-15 pixels of vertical screen space. 

Which application should I use to do this?

I've tried conky but I can't get the text/bars close enough to the top of the screen (even with gap_x 0 gap_y 0) and the maximum width option doesn't allow me to stretch conky wide enough for anymore than about two statistics (maximum_width won't go any wider than roughly 500 pixels. I need 1440).

What other apps could I use?

---

### Post by meborc on 2008-08-09

> It's not a mockup.

---

### Post by easybake on 2008-08-09
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> Okay, got question.

Lets say I want to have system stats (CPU usage; memory usage; disk usage) along the very top of my screen. I don't want it to appear above other windows, nor do I want it to take up anymore than 12-15 pixels of vertical screen space. 

Which application should I use to do this?

I've tried conky but I can't get the text/bars close enough to the top of the screen (even with gap_x 0 gap_y 0) and the maximum width option doesn't allow me to stretch conky wide enough for anymore than about two statistics (maximum_width won't go any wider than roughly 500 pixels. I need 1440).

What other apps could I use?

In conky you can always use the $voffset variable. Without a gap value you should be able to move the text right to the edge of the screen. Use something like ```
${voffset -8}
```
If you are running into max width problems just launch 2 different conkys.

---

### Post by sunexplodes on 2008-08-12
Here's mine. 

I've combined 3 themes to make my GTK theme (Elegant Aurora and Glow, with the panel.rc from Wobed), plus a few cosmetic changes to make it all fit together nicely. I then modified the Aurora Elegant Emerald theme to make it work with my colour scheme. 

I've attached both for anyone who's interested.

PS: I'd also like to mention that the original "Glow" theme is made by our own "What Is In A Name?" and is excellent, in that it weeds out all the crappy stuff about the Aurora engine and looks just excellent. ### Post by JillSwift on 2008-08-12
> **aristotlewilde said:**
> Love the conky!  Mind sharing?Love to =^_^=
```
own_window yes
own_window_type normal
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
draw_graph_borders no

# Use double buffering (reduces flicker, may not work for everyone)
double_buffer yes

# fiddle with window
use_xft yes
xftfont Eurostile:size=10
xftalpha 0.6

# Update interval in seconds
update_interval 1.00

# Minimum size of text area
minimum_size 10 5
# maximum_width 250

# Draw shades?
draw_shades no

# Text stuff
draw_outline yes # amplifies text if yes
draw_borders no
uppercase no # set to yes if you want all text to be in uppercase

# border margins
border_margin 1

# border width
border_width 1

# Default colors and also border colors, grey90 == #e5e5e5
default_color white

# Text alignment
alignment middle_right

# Gap between borders of screen and text
gap_x 2
gap_y 2

# stuff after 'TEXT' will be formatted on screen

TEXT
${color yellow}SYSTEM ${hr 3}${color 3590ff}
${font Elementary:size=32}${alignc 0}${time %A}$font
${font Elementary:size=24}${alignc 0}${time %D}$font
${font Elementary:size=43}${alignc 0}${time %I:%M %p}${font Monotype.com:size=3}$color

$font${alignc 0}$nodename on $machine
${alignc 0}$sysname $kernel
${alignc 0}Uptime: $uptime
${color yellow}CPU ${hr 3}$color
Pentium D ${freq}MHz${alignr}Temp:${acpitemp}C ($acpifan)
${color ff6600}${cpubar 10}$color
${cpugraph cpu1 25,122 ff9900 ff99aa}${alignr 0}${cpugraph cpu2 25,122 00ff99 aaff99}
${color}Processes:$processes  ${alignr}Running:$running_processes
${font Monotype.com:size=6}NAME ${alignc 0}CPU% $alignr MEM%
${top name 1} ${alignc 0}${top cpu 1} $alignr ${top mem 1}
${top name 2} ${alignc 0}${top cpu 2} $alignr ${top mem 2}
${top name 3} ${alignc 0}${top cpu 3} $alignr ${top mem 3}
${top name 4} ${alignc 0}${top cpu 4} $alignr ${top mem 4}
${top name 5} ${alignc 0}${top cpu 5} $alignr ${top mem 5}${font Monotype.com:size=3}

$font${color yellow}MEMORY / DISK USAGE ${hr 3}$color
${color cyan}RAM:${mem} ${alignc}$memperc% ${alignr}Swap:${swap}
${membar 6}
${color}/root:  ${fs_free /}${alignr}${fs_size /}
${fs_bar 6 /}$color 
/home:  ${fs_free /home}${alignr}${fs_size /home}
${fs_bar 6 /home}$color${font Monotype.com:size=3}

$font${color yellow}NETWORK ${font Arial Narrow:size=8}(${color green}${addr eth0}${color yellow}) (${color orange}${tail /**[COLOR=Red]path_to_[/COLOR]**/wanip.txt 2}${color yellow}) ${hr 3}$font$color
Down:${downspeedf eth0}k/s ${alignr}Up:${upspeedf eth0}k/s
${downspeedgraph eth0 30,122 ffff00 ff0000} ${alignr}${upspeedgraph eth0 30,122 00ffff 00ff00}$color
Total Downloaded: ${totaldown eth0}
```On login, this script fetches the WAN address:
```
#!/bin/bash
wget http://whatismyip.org/ -O /**[COLOR=Red]path_to_[/COLOR]**/wanip.txt
exec 3< /**[COLOR=Red]path_to_[/COLOR]**/wanip.txt
read <&3 ip
kdialog --msgbox "Our WAN IP address is: $ip" --title "WAN IP Address" &
exit 0
```Enjoy! :)

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-08-14
> **dbbolton said:**
> Could you post your gtk_color_scheme ?


Sure. In fact, I'm posting the whole theme and the Metacity correspondent, since the color scheme wasn't the only change in the theme. The colors will probably be further tweaked, but as for now, this is how the theme is.

See, I'm thinking of creating a new Glow series, a sort of Deluxe edition where the suite of themes will look like it's the GTK version of a chocolate box. Unlike the previous Glow, each theme will have some unique tweaks here and there, so the colours won't be the only change. I'm thinking of a Cocoa theme, a Vanilla theme, an After Eight one, there's this sort of Caramel-ish theme, the one I'm uploading, inspired in New Human and WillWill's famous mockup, and probably I'll do something of the likes of the Kin color scheme.

EDIT: Oh, and for the one who asked, I'm using the Gnome-Human icon set.

It's available through the following link at GNOME-Look.org: [http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/The+Unofficial+Widget+Factory+(DEB)?content=84209](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/The+Unofficial+Widget+Factory+(DEB)?content=84209)

Thank you again.  Unfortunately, I need the source so that I can build it on Gentoo.  I sent a very polite email to the author asking for it, or for a link to be added to it at gnome-look.org.  Hopefully it will be available soon.  :)

### Post by picpak on 2008-08-14
> **Stan_1936 said:**
> Could you please post your conky setup?

Also what font are you using?  The normal Clearlooks-Evolving theme font?

Conky:

```
#avoid flicker
double_buffer yes

#own window to run simultanious 2 or more conkys
own_window  yes
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_type desktop
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager 

#borders
draw_borders no
border_margin 1

#shades
draw_shades no

#position
gap_x 6
gap_y 36
alignment top_left

#behaviour
update_interval 10

#colour
default_color  cccccc

#default_shade_color 000000
#own_window_colour 3d352a

#font
use_xft yes
xftfont HandelGotDLig:pixelsize=12

#to prevent window from moving
use_spacer none
minimum_size 1024 0

TEXT
${alignc}Kernel ${color bbbbbb}$kernel   |  ${color}Date ${color bbbbbb}${time %B %d %I:%M}  |  ${color}Cpu ${color bbbbbb}${cpu}%   |   ${color }Mem ${color bbbbbb}$mem/$memmax - $memperc%   |   ${color}Swp ${color bbbbbb}$swap/$swapmax - $swapperc%   
${alignc} ${color }Root ${color bbbbbb}${font}${fs_used /}  / ${fs_size /} - ${fs_used_perc /}%   |  ${color}Uptime ${color bbbbbb}${uptime}   | ${color}Processes ${color bbbbbb}$processes   | ${color}Running ${color bbbbbb}$running_processes   
```

The titlebar font is Lucida Grande Bold.

### Post by kamitsukai on 2008-08-14
> **billgoldberg said:**
> Those big dates and that system info above the bird, is that conky?

I would love to see those conkyrc files, if you feel like sharing.

well the dates are in fact a theme for the Wallpaper Clock Screenlet which you can find here ([http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php?content=66717](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php?content=66717))
And here's the theme Configuration I used ([http://www.vladstudio.com/wallpaperclock/details.php?80)](http://www.vladstudio.com/wallpaperclock/details.php?80)) although I've just found out theres a bug which produces some random black rectangle at the bottom of the screen sometimes ([http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=890116](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=890116)) don't know whats causing it yet but I think it might be were conky refreshes:confused:
[U]
conkyrc:[/U]

```
alignment top_right

cpu_avg_samples 2
net_avg_samples 2
update_interval 1

default_color white
default_outline_color white
default_shade_color white

draw_borders no
draw_shades no

border_margin 7
border_width 1

gap_x 225
gap_y 150

maximum_width 264

use_xft yes
xftfont heroin07-12
xftalpha 0.8

own_window yes
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager

use_spacer yes
double_buffer yes
no_buffers yes

CC0066
TEXT


${color white}${font marvosym:size=14}U ${font}${color #CCCCCC}$uptime up

${color white}${font marvosym:size=14}A ${font}${color #888888}cpu:  ${color #CCCCCC}${cpu}%
${color white}${font weather:size=14}y ${font}${color #888888}temp: ${color #CCCCCC}${acpitemp}C

${color white}${font marvosym:size=14}j ${font}${color #888888}ram : ${color #CCCCCC}$memperc% 
${color white}${font marvosym:size=14}h ${font}${color #888888}swap: ${color #CCCCCC}$swapperc%

${color white}/  ${color #888888}root : ${color #CCCCCC}${fs_free_perc /}% 
${color white}${font webdings:size=14}Ã ${font}${color #888888}home : ${color #CCCCCC}${fs_free_perc /home/carl}% 
${color white}${font webdings:size=14}Í ${font}${color #888888}altr : ${color #CCCCCC}${fs_free_perc /media/comun}% 

${if_existing /proc/net/route eth0}${color white}${font webdings:size=14}ø ${font}${color #CCCCCC}${font Heroin 07:size=16}${addr eth0}
${color white}${font wingdings:size=14}Ú ${font}${color #CCCCCC}${downspeed eth0}k/s
${color white}${font wingdings:size=14}Ò ${font}${color #CCCCCC}${upspeed eth0}k/s${endif}
${if_existing /proc/net/route ath0}${color white}${font webdings:size=14}ø ${font}${color #CCCCCC}${font size=10}${addr ath0}
${color white}${font wingdings:size=14}Ú ${font}${color #CCCCCC}${downspeed ath0}k/s

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-08-14
> **indecisive said:**
> What is in a name?, how can I get the Aurora GTK engine?  When I apply your theme, it looks ugly, and the widgets are all just boxes, unlike yours.

Hi there!

You can either get the source code from the following link, and then compile it (it was what I did): [http://xfce-look.org/content/show.php?content=56438](http://xfce-look.org/content/show.php?content=56438)

Or, for instance, get the Futurelooks set of themes from here: [http://futurelooks.googlecode.com/files/Futurelooks2.0.tar.gz](http://futurelooks.googlecode.com/files/Futurelooks2.0.tar.gz)
It contains a .deb package with the Aurora engine, inside of a folder called "FutureAurora". Installing Aurora from there might be more practical, and cleaner too.

EDIT: We could also try to convince the author of the engine to keep developing it and/or to let others help him out, so that Aurora's bugs can finally be fixed and the engine can go to our repos after some time.

---

### Post by Giant Speck on 2008-08-14
> **What is in a name? said:**
> Hi there!

You can either get the source code from the following link, and then compile it (it was what I did): [http://xfce-look.org/content/show.php?content=56438](http://xfce-look.org/content/show.php?content=56438)

Or, for instance, get the Futurelooks set of themes from here: [http://futurelooks.googlecode.com/files/Futurelooks2.0.tar.gz](http://futurelooks.googlecode.com/files/Futurelooks2.0.tar.gz)
It contains a .deb package with the Aurora engine, inside of a folder called "FutureAurora". Installing Aurora from there might be more practical, and cleaner too.

EDIT: We could also try to convince the author of the engine to keep developing it and/or to let others help him out, so that Aurora's bugs can finally be fixed and the engine can go to our repos after some time.

1.  What is the font you use in your screenshots?

2.  Do you know how to fix the ugly buttons problem in Firefox?  Or what browser do you use?

---

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-08-14
> **Giant Speck said:**
> 1.  What is the font you use in your screenshots?

2.  Do you know how to fix the ugly buttons problem in Firefox?  Or what browser do you use?

1. I use Calibri, bold, size 8;

2. Aurora itself has some bugs itself, and the way Firefox tries to impersonate the GTK widgets is far from perfect too. That said, I guess you would have a cleaner looking browser if you used Epiphany, which is GNOME's browser anyway, or some others. I personally use Firefox and try to ignore the borders around the buttons and address bars. After all, OpenOffice looks even worse in that regard, so, what to do?

I'd gladly use only the more supported engines, especially Clearlooks and some interesting resources from the SVN versions of Murrine, but honestly, is there any other engine from which you can get those soft yet well defined, solid, smooth and delicious buttons you get with Aurora? Clearlooks would be the closest competitor. It fails in some little details. But then Aurora has BUGS... So frustrating.

---

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2008-08-14
Conky enthusiasts, lend me your brains:

[[img]http://img530.imageshack.us/img530/1096/arghconkysmallkx1.png[/img]](http://img141.imageshack.us/img141/7307/arghconkyfullzv5.png)

```
#by endel /endel@tlen.pl/
background yes

use_xft yes
# xft font when Xft is enabled
xftfont kroeger 05_55 caps:size=7
override_utf8_locale yes

# Text alpha when using Xft
xftalpha 1

update_interval 1
use_xft yes
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
stippled_borders no
border_margin 0
border_width 0
default_color 779dae
default_shade_color black
default_outline_color grey
own_window yes
own_window_transparent no
own_window_type normal
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
own_window_colour 151515
alignment top_middle
#alignment top_right
#alignment bottom_left
#alignment bottom_right
gap_x 0
gap_y 0
no_buffers yes
uppercase no
double_buffer yes
use_spacer no
minimum_size 1440 0
mail_spool $HOME/Maildir/



TEXT
    ${font} Cpu: ${color E7E7E7}${font}	${cpubar 4,100}	${color} Mem: ${color E7E7E7}${font}	${membar 4,100}${color}	| Net: ${color E7E7E7}${font}	${downspeed eth0} Kb/s ${color}	${totaldown eth0} down${color}	| ${color E7E7E7}	${upspeed eth0} Kb/s ${color}	${totalup eth0} up${color}	|  File System: ${color E7E7E7}${font}	${fs_free /} ${color}	Win HDD: ${color E7E7E7}${font}	${fs_free /media/windows_drive} ${color}	Share HDD: ${color E7E7E7}${font}	${fs_free /media/shared_drive} ${color}	| Email: ${color E7E7E7}	${execi 60 perl ~/Skrypty/gmail.pl n} new messages ${color}	| Weather:  ${color E7E7E7}${font}	${execi 1800 $HOME/Skrypty/pogodynka.sh}${color}	| Top:  ${color E7E7E7}${font}	${top name 1}${top name 2}
${voffset -11}${alignr 10}${color E7E7E7}${time %e} ${color}${time %B}

```


Edit: NM, just figured it out: own_window_type desktop

Edit edit: don't suppose Xft supports hinting now, does it?

### Post by rjmdomingo2003 on 2008-08-15
> **Killeroid said:**
> Can you post your .tintrc please?

Sure.

```
#---------------------------------------------
# TINT CONFIG FILE
#---------------------------------------------

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL
#---------------------------------------------
panel_mode = multi_desktop
panel_monitor = 1
panel_position = bottom right
panel_size = 1276 20
panel_margin = 2 2
panel_padding = 4 4
font_shadow = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
panel_rounded = 0
panel_border_width = 0
panel_background_color = #1b1b1b 100
panel_border_color = #ffffff 90

#---------------------------------------------
# TASKS
#---------------------------------------------
task_text_centered = 1
task_width = 90
task_margin = 3
task_padding = 5
task_icon_size = 0
task_font = Audimat 7
task_font_color = #ffffff 15
task_active_font_color = #52a8c1 100

#---------------------------------------------
# TASK BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
task_rounded = 3
task_background_color = #000000 0
task_active_background_color = #000000 0
task_border_width = 0
task_border_color = #ffffff 18
task_active_border_color = #ffffff 70

#---------------------------------------------
# CLOCK
#---------------------------------------------
time1_format = %H:%M  %A  %d %B %Y
time1_font = Audimat 7
#time2_format = %A %d %B %Y
#time2_font = Audimat 7
clock_font_color = #52a8c1 100

#---------------------------------------------
# MOUSE ACTION ON TASK
#---------------------------------------------
mouse_middle = none
mouse_right = close
mouse_scroll_up = toggle
mouse_scroll_down = iconify


```

Well, thanks for the compliment!

As for what you said concerning the Ubuntu Wiki, I do realise that Ubuntu's artwork team seems to be very very conservative and nit-picky. But then again, most of the ideas at the Wiki aren't feasible at all (except for some ideas which could be done using the pixbuf engine, and this isn't perfect either). How many already done themes are published there? I guess the default themes in Ubuntu will always be done either in Clearlooks or in Murrine (or mixing both), and neither of these two engines does many of the über-modern things people post after their personal brainstorms. That is very limitating and also very frustrating if you have more advanced ideas. Aurora, for instance, is seldom updated. Both Murrine and Clearlooks are nowadays in the hands of Andrea Cimitan, and I believe that one person can't do all the work alone.

### Post by picpak on 2008-08-15
> **Stan_1936 said:**
> **No, I don't think there's need for that.**  However, what did you mean by "The titlebar font is Lucida Grande Bold."  What's the difference between the titlebar font and the Mac font that you are using?  Where are they being used and how are they different.  Sorry if thhis sounds trivial..I'm new.

Well the font for my programs is Segoe UI, and the font for my titlebars is Lucida Grande Bold. Lucida Grande Bold is a Mac font, Segoe UI is a Vista font.

I should also note that I'm using Openbox, not GNOME (the default Ubuntu desktop environment). In GNOME, you would go to **System** > **Preferences** > **Appearance**, click on the **Fonts** tab, and change "Window title font" to Lucida Grande Bold. Hope this helps!

---

### Post by yabbadabbadont on 2008-08-15
> **Stan_1936 said:**
> Do you mean I'll have to download it first or something?

In your conky setup, you simply had:

```
xftfont HandelGotDLig:pixelsize=12
```

Do I need to download this to a particular location first?

I'm using Xubuntu(XFCE).

[http://www.fontica.com/font/handelgotdlig](http://www.fontica.com/font/handelgotdlig)

Download the ttf file (truetype font) and put it into the ".fonts" directory in your home directory.  Note: the name starts with a period, so it is hidden by default.  Also, you may have to create the ".fonts" directory.  Finally, you will need to log out and back in probably before the font will show up.

---

### Post by Stan_1936 on 2008-08-15
> **yabbadabbadont said:**
> [http://www.fontica.com/font/handelgotdlig](http://www.fontica.com/font/handelgotdlig)

Download the ttf file (truetype font) and put it into the ".fonts" directory in your home directory.  Note: the name starts with a period, so it is hidden by default.  Also, you may have to create the ".fonts" directory.  Finally, you will need to log out and back in probably before the font will show up.

---

### Post by yabbadabbadont on 2008-08-15
> **Stan_1936 said:**
> Thanks a lot.  Did you mean I will have to put it in this directory: /home/.fonts?

No, your user's home directory.  For example, my user is daffy, so it would be placed in: /home/daffy/.fonts

---

### Post by Stan_1936 on 2008-08-15
Is that also the same with /.themes and /.icons?

I thought that for /.themes, it would be /usr/share/.themes

---

### Post by yabbadabbadont on 2008-08-15
> **Stan_1936 said:**
> Is that also the same with /.themes and /.icons?

Yes.

Edit: The global theme and icon directories are /usr/share/themes and /usr/share/icons.  Your personal directories are /home/username/.themes and /home/username/.icons

---

### Post by andrek on 2008-08-16
> **71CH said:**
> I did a search but couldn't find much on tint.  Can somebody explain how I can install/use it?  Thanks.

Download sources from [http://code.google.com/p/tint2/](http://code.google.com/p/tint2/) and build them. Then, open tint for a while ( so that it can create it's config files ) and kill it. Open /home/username/.config/tint/tintrc and paste there content from [http://pastebin.com/fdf82128](http://pastebin.com/fdf82128)
Then you can add tint to your autostart scripts.

### Post by picpak on 2008-08-16

---

### Post by Giant Speck on 2008-08-16
> **el mariachi said:**
> if the web was black, we would save a lot of electricity :D

That is mostly false.

On an LCD display, it takes just as much energy to display a predominantly black screen than it does to display a predominantly white screen.  Even if there was an energy savings occurring, it would be so minuscule that we wouldn't benefit from it.

On CRT (cathode ray tube) displays, however, you would see an energy savings of 5% to 20%.

Either way, a more feasible way to save energy with your monitor would be to adjust the contrast and brightness settings.

---

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2008-08-16
> **the yawner said:**
> I've been learning a bit on modifying a clearlooks gtk theme by trial and error. But I've no clue on how (if it's possible) this can be achieved in Gnome.

[IMG]http://img.photobucket.com/albums/v90/kiel_008/Xfce-Panel.png[/IMG]

Note: It's a Xfce panel with option _use flat buttons_ enabled.

Care to point me on a working theme that has this? Thanks in advance.

The only way I can think of would be to use the pixmap engine for GtkButton widgets, in a sub-style for only panels. Eg, something like:

```
widget_class "*Panel*" style "panel"
widget "*Panel*" style "panel"
class "*Panel*" style "panel"

style "panel"
{
engine "pixmap"
engine "pixmap"
  {
    image
    {
      function			= BOX
      detail				= "buttondefault"
      recolorable		= TRUE
      file				= "Buttons/button-default.png"
      border			= {4, 4, 4, 4}
      stretch			= TRUE
    }
    image
    {
      function			= BOX
      state				= PRELIGHT
      recolorable		= TRUE
      file				= "Buttons/button-prelight.png"
      border			= { 4, 4, 4, 4 }
      stretch			= TRUE
    }
    image
    {
      function			= BOX
      state				= ACTIVE
      file				= "Buttons/button-pressed.png"
      border			= { 4, 4, 4, 4 }
      stretch			= TRUE
    }	
    image 
   {
     function			= BOX
     state				= INSENSITIVE
     file					= "Buttons/button-insensitive.png"
     border			= { 4, 4, 4, 4 }
     stretch			= TRUE
    }
    image 
    {
      function			= BOX
      file				= "Buttons/button-normal.png"		
      border			= { 4, 4, 4, 4 }
      stretch			= TRUE
     }	
  }
}

```

Just make sure your ACTIVE button image is basically just a plain white png.

---

### Post by perfectska04@hotmail.com on 2008-08-17
> **the yawner said:**
> I've been learning a bit on modifying a clearlooks gtk theme by trial and error. But I've no clue on how (if it's possible) this can be achieved in Gnome.

[IMG]http://img.photobucket.com/albums/v90/kiel_008/Xfce-Panel.png[/IMG]

Note: It's a Xfce panel with option _use flat buttons_ enabled.

Care to point me on a working theme that has this? Thanks in advance.

Flat buttons should be really easy to get in GNOME without having to modify any theme. Just right click a panel, and select "properties". In the Background tab, choose a background image you would want to use for your panel, and as a result, unfocused items will not look like a button, but part of the panel itself.

---

### Post by merlyn on 2008-08-17
Here's my current effort.

I'm trying to set up a dark desktop that is both visually appealing and functional.

There are some tweaks that I need to work on, but it seems to be coming along.

Also I'm open to suggestions for icon themes that suit dark / black desktops, that fit the following requirements,

1) are complete / near complete and,

2) don't require hacking to get working, i.e setting up links or editing the index.theme.

Details are as follows;

Wallpaper: [Growing Love]("http://minimaster184.deviantart.com/art/Growing-Love-64435402") by MiniMaster

GTK 2+: [Bling Noir]("http://umarmung.deviantart.com/art/Bling-Noir-47689233") by umar mung, I'm trying to figure out how to change some of the colours, as the theme engine used does not allow for this. Some text / element colours make reading a little difficult.

Emerald: [Overglossed]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Overglossed+Emerald?content=74873") by TheRob, I've changed the colour for the title bar fonts & shadows to fit with other theme elements.

Icons: [GlassDark]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/GlassDark?content=82404") by mtax & [Tango-noir]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Tango-noir?content=38964") by wedderburn, the author has stated that GlassDark is currently a preview, so I've added the line Inherits=tango-noir into it's index.theme to fill in some gaps.

Panel: Set to solid colour, slider to full transparancy

Cheers.

---

### Post by Truedream on 2008-08-18
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> Conkyrc please. I'd really like to find out how you've stopped percentages changing from single to double digits without screwing up the alignment of other objects on the same line.


use ${goto xxx} code.

here is my conkyrc

```

TEXT
${font zekton:size=8}Total Down:${color orange} ${totaldown eth0} $color ${goto 130}Total Up:${color orange} ${totalup eth0} $color ${goto 250}CPU Temp: ${color orange}${execi 2 cat /sys/bus/pci/drivers/k8temp/000*/temp1_input | cut -c1,2}&#730;C/${execi 2 cat /sys/bus/pci/drivers/k8temp/000*/temp3_input | cut -c1,2}&#730;C${color} ${goto 370} HDD/Chip: ${color orange} $alignr ${execi 300 nc localhost 7634 | cut -b26-27 ;}&#730;C/${execi 60 nvidia-settings -query GPUCoreTemp | perl -ne 'print $1 if /GPUCoreTemp.*?: (\d+)./;'}&#730;C $color
CPU1: ${color orange}${cpu cpu1}% $color ${goto 130}CPU2: ${color orange}${cpu cpu2}% $color ${goto 250}RAM: ${color orange}$memperc%  ${mem} ${color}${goto 370} Downstream:${color orange}$alignr${downspeed eth0} Kb/s $color
${color1}${cpubar cpu1 5,110} ${goto 130}${color2}${cpubar cpu2 5,110} ${goto 250}${color3}${membar 5,110} ${color}${goto 370} Upstream:   ${color orange}$alignr${upspeed eth0} Kb/s $color
```

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2008-08-18
> **merlyn said:**
> Here's my current effort.

I'm trying to set up a dark desktop that is both visually appealing and functional.

There are some tweaks that I need to work on, but it seems to be coming along.

Also I'm open to suggestions for icon themes that suit dark / black desktops, that fit the following requirements,
You don't need a dark icon theme to go with the rest of your system. Hell, even the vanilla tango icon theme looks better on a dark system than it does on a light system; the colours looks more saturated.

Also, this may sound counter-intuitive but your wallpaper shouldn't be completely black like that. Firstly, you want some contrast between open windows and the background, for both usability and aesthetic reasons. Secondly, if you've been working in a *completely* dark environment and then you suddenly open up a white webpage, you're going to be blinded. You need to minimise the amount of adaptation your eyes need to do. By having a lighter background (not real light but at least slightly brighter than charcoal tones), your peripheral vision takes care of this.

Edit: I realise you've already noticed this but I'll mention it anyway; text should not be #ffffff. It's a blight. I generally use a maximum white tone of #bfbfbf.

---

xwinwrap -ni -o 0.6 -fs -s -nf -sp -- mplayer -wid WID -quiet '/MEDIA FILE'
```

Oh... and the coolest thing of all shown in the last image, the cute little MOVIE.WATERMARK script on my desktop that runs movies, click through and transparency so you can watch your movie, do your work and eat it too!

Very well said. I only used OSX on a sound gig a few years ago and I'm glad to be able to run Mac4Lin on my Ubuntu box. I think the main reason I love Mac4Lin is because it gets my comp away from the Windows look (I feel) that comes in Ubuntu, plus I like some of the icons. One day I'll make a nice theme that borrows from the best of both Linux and OSX but in the mean time I really like being able to choose how my system works. And if it weren't for Mac4Lin and Google Gadgets there's no telling how long it would have taken me to find both a dock and a sidebar that I like. Now I just wish I had a good way to use both Google's sidebar gadgets and some Screenlets, but the WeatherBug sidebar won't run outside of Google and I really like having an analog clock at the top of my sidebar.

Of course my desktop, like most, is a work in progress so any month my desktop can change looks dramatically.

### Post by aristotlewilde on 2008-08-19
> **Stan_1936 said:**

As an added bonus, you get a lot more comfortable w/ the command line.

### Post by Nepherte on 2008-08-19
It's called Global Menu, the former mac style menu bar. You can find info on it here: [https://wiki.ubuntu.com/global_menu](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/global_menu)

### Post by LeoSolaris on 2008-08-19
[quote=Toupee]
Just out of curiosity, how do you separate the toolbar from the window like that? I mean, I realize that's the OSX way, but I always thought it was silly and not very functional.[/quote]
It's just a dock bar. That one looks like simdock, but it could be one of the others, like kiba, cairo, or AWN.


Edit: Ohh! My bad, I wasn't looking hard enough. I see what your talking about now. Nepherte has it right. Ya... that looks like too much work for something that relatively useless. Besides, it doesn't look tidy to me.

---

### Post by darksizzle on 2008-08-19
> **Toupee said:**
> 
Just out of curiosity, how do you separate the toolbar from the window like that?  I mean, I realize that's the OSX way, but I always thought it was silly and not very functional. ;)

Actually with the way that OS X groups an application's windows together (an alt tab in os x will tab through applications and not through windows) it's a good way to keep track of the windows you have in that application throughout the workspaces.  Plus it saves window space (not much but any bit helps).  Would you rather have one menu for each of your 5 open terminals or a global menu in the top bar you're going to have anyway.

---

### Post by darksizzle on 2008-08-19
> **LeoSolaris said:**
> It's just a dock bar. That one looks like simdock, but it could be one of the others, like kiba, cairo, or AWN.

He was asking about the global menu applet that I'm using.  The dock is cairo-dock which is pretty nice.  It's closest to the behavior of os x and allows you to put it on the side of the screen which awn isn't capable of.

### Post by Toupee on 2008-08-19
Thanks all for answering my question. 

> **darksizzle said:**
> Actually with the way that OS X groups an application's windows together (an alt tab in os x will tab through applications and not through windows) it's a good way to keep track of the windows you have in that application throughout the workspaces.  Plus it saves window space (not much but any bit helps).  Would you rather have one menu for each of your 5 open terminals or a global menu in the top bar you're going to have anyway.

I would much rather have one menu for each open window.  Say Window A isn't in focus, and I want to access the Tools menu.  I have to first click Window A before the menu is even available, then move my cursor to the top of the screen.  What's the point in that?  If the toolbars are attached to the windows, I can just click Tools right away in Window A.  And I don't have to move my cursor all over the place. :)

(While I'm OSX-ranting, why the hell can't you resize a window from any side or corner?  Darn stupid.)

---

I would much rather have one menu for each open window.  Say Window A isn't in focus, and I want to access the Tools menu.  I have to first click Window A before the menu is even available, then move my cursor to the top of the screen.  What's the point in that?  If the toolbars are attached to the windows, I can just click Tools right away in Window A.  And I don't have to move my cursor all over the place. :)

(While I'm OSX-ranting, why the hell can't you resize a window from any side or corner?  Darn stupid.)

Yeah I usually alt-tab through my windows and use the menu keybinding so I don't hit that issue.  Keybindings are awesome!  I hear yah on the resize crap. I think it gives a cleaner look with the menu missing from all the windows.  To each their own!

### Post by aaaantoine on 2008-08-20
Hoo boy, I've been putting this one together for the past couple of days.  I went from a 1280x24 top panel + 1280x48 auto-hidden bottom panel to a single 32x800 left panel to maximize vertical proportions.  While I was at it, I decided to redo my entire theme.

**WM:** Gnome
**Background:** Found somewhere on the Internet a while back. (copy attached)
**GTK:** [Compact-Colors](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Compact-Colors?content=78182), with custom color scheme, and default panel background removed.
**Border:** [Almond](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Almond+(5+version)?content=39632) (Metacity) 
**App Font:** [Latin Modern](http://www.gust.org.pl/projects/e-foundry/latin-modern) Sans 8pt
**Border Font:** Sans Bold 8pt.
**Icons:** [Ultimate Gnome](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Ultimate+Gnome?content=75000)
**Panel Background:** A glossy, semi translucent home built 32x32 graphic for vertical panel use. (copy attached)
**Clock:** Gnome Screenlets clock.

### Post by aaaantoine on 2008-08-20
> **voteforpedro36 said:**
> For some reason I can't stand side vertical panels. But it's great, if that works for you. One thing though, how do you manage minimized windows? Sorry if it seems I'm complaining, I'm not, your screen shot is great, and I'm bored and want something to talk about.

I don't really know if this works for me or not, yet.  I've tried a different variation of it in the past, but I caved due to old habits.  At the time, I was still using Windows.  Aesthetically, I do think it's rather ugly.  It's more about function than form.
  
As for managing minimized windows, I have a few methods available to me at any time.

1. (Mouse Access 1) The icon just below the first separator is a Window Selector applet (if you have Gnome, it's one of the stock applets).  I can click that show a list of all available windows, regardless of workspace.  I have to do this instead of a task list because the task list is nearly useless on a vertical panel.

2. (Mouse Access 2: compositing) If I click in the bottom right corner I reveal all applications.  I originally set this when I had a dock at the bottom, but I never got rid of it, despite barely using it.

3. (Keyboard Access) Alt-Tab lets me switch windows in the current workspace. Super-Tab lets me switch to a window from any workspace.

I might try playing with a second vertical panel for quicker access to all my usual apps.

---

Anyways, here is the new theme:

GDM:                ArchDarch
Gtk2:                Mesmerize (Gnome-look.org)
Colors:              tweaked to suit the theme

Icons:               Glass Icons (GL.o)
Pointer:             Chameleon-Anthracite-Small (Gl.o)
AWN:                Personalized theme

FF3 theme:       Aquatint Black Gloss (Addons)

### Post by voteforpedro36 on 2008-08-21
> **aaaantoine said:**
> I don't really know if this works for me or not, yet.  I've tried a different variation of it in the past, but I caved due to old habits.  At the time, I was still using Windows.  Aesthetically, I do think it's rather ugly.  It's more about function than form.
  
As for managing minimized windows, I have a few methods available to me at any time.

1. (Mouse Access 1) The icon just below the first separator is a Window Selector applet (if you have Gnome, it's one of the stock applets).  I can click that show a list of all available windows, regardless of workspace.  I have to do this instead of a task list because the task list is nearly useless on a vertical panel.

2. (Mouse Access 2: compositing) If I click in the bottom right corner I reveal all applications.  I originally set this when I had a dock at the bottom, but I never got rid of it, despite barely using it.

3. (Keyboard Access) Alt-Tab lets me switch windows in the current workspace. Super-Tab lets me switch to a window from any workspace.

I might try playing with a second vertical panel for quicker access to all my usual apps.

The thing that would bother me is not being able to see ALL the open windows at one time, the window selector applet is close, but even then, you must click it to see every available window. Albeit I do use Alt-Tab a lot even when I have a panel, but I like to be able to see my changes in window. But that's probably just me being weird :D.

> **DJ_Peng said:**
> @voteforpedro36:

I forgot to multi-quote you and I haven't had all of my first cup of coffee yet. I think my brain is still trying to finish booting.)

Yeah, he definitely deserves a break.

And herbster, that's nice, I always like your screenshots. What is the task manager/panel at the top? I believe it's the first time you haven't had one of those big desert pictures as your wall. :)

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-08-21
[[IMG]http://c.imagehost.org/t/0537/ecra.jpg[/IMG]](http://c.imagehost.org/view/0537/ecra.png) [[IMG]http://c.imagehost.org/t/0697/ecra2.jpg[/IMG]](http://c.imagehost.org/view/0697/ecra2.png) [[IMG]http://c.imagehost.org/t/0131/ecra3.jpg[/IMG]](http://c.imagehost.org/view/0131/ecra3.png)

Hello everybody!
It's wonderful to know when people care for us that much and like what we do, thank you so much! I used to be at a University, studying Journalism, but meanwhile I had to drop it for several reasons, money included, and I'm also unemployed at the moment, so my coffee breaks are not glamorous at all. Sometimes I go a bit more quiet when my head needs to have a rest from developing artwork and learning, testing, tweaking and debugging code from 20+ themes, plus reading and trying to answer quite a few comments, personal messages and e-mails (some of them comparing my work to the Windows 2000 look, which is absolutely great for my ego; but then again, ego is an illusion). It's a bit overwhelming at times. Having a depression like I do is like being in a rollercoaster, but I like to at least try to be useful to the community when I have some energy and some ideas to keep me going. And believe me, I hate it when I get slower doing some stuff, because people need an answer or some sort of help (and sometimes I get too forgetful, which is not good either). Or when I get too aggressive anyway.

So, here I am, listening to Rodrigo Leão, one of the best musicians in the world (to me, at least), reading the news about Nelson Évora at the Olympic Games and trying to relax, disconnect myself from what's around me and to get inspired to write something. I miss my poetry. Either that or reading some stuff about spirituality, philosophy, psychology, arts, whatever appears first.

The details of the screenshots above:
Wallpaper: "OpalescentWS", which came in the pack of wallpapers by Ether that someone mentioned some pages ago;
Icon set: "Eikon", which I'm still trying to perfect, step by step;
GTK and Metacity: K03, the no-borders version; I also toned down the window's background color from #FFFFFF to #EDEDED.

I'm also trying out a different look for Firefox. Since Clearlooks looks weird when it comes to having light widgets over a dark background (Aurora isn't the only engine with issues, hint hint), I decided to disable the Tiny menu extension for a while, move the address and the search fields to the Navigation bar and leave the full menu on the right of the browser, with the back/forward/refresh/homepage buttons on the left. Looks neat. To me, at least.

---

### Post by billgoldberg on 2008-08-21
My new fluxbox setup.

That conky setup took me hours to perfect.

The conkyrc file:

> background yes
use_xft yes
xftfont 123:size=8
xftalpha 0.1
update_interval 0.5
total_run_times 0
own_window yes
own_window_type normal
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
double_buffer yes
minimum_size 250 5
maximum_width 400
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders no
default_color gray
default_shade_color red
default_outline_color green
alignment top_right
gap_x 10
gap_y 10
no_buffers no
uppercase no
cpu_avg_samples 2
net_avg_samples 1
override_utf8_locale yes
use_spacer yes
text_buffer_size 256

TEXT

               ${font openlogos:size=20}U${font Arial:size=20}${color Tan1}GNU${color Ivory}LINUX${font openlogos:size=20}t

${voffset -90}
${color DimGray}
${font}
${font Arial:bold:size=10}${color Tan1}SYSTEM ${color DarkSlateGray} ${hr 2}
$font${color DimGray}$sysname $kernel $alignr $machine
Intel Pentium D $alignr${freq_g cpu0}Ghz
Uptime $alignr${uptime}
File System $alignr${fs_type}

${font Arial:bold:size=10}${color Tan1}PROCESSORS ${color DarkSlateGray}${hr 2}
$font${color DimGray}CPU1  ${cpu cpu1}% ${cpubar cpu1}
CPU2  ${cpu cpu2}% ${cpubar cpu2}

${font Arial:bold:size=10}${color Tan1}MEMORY ${color DarkSlateGray}${hr 2}
$font${color DimGray}MEM $alignc $mem / $memmax $alignr $memperc%
$membar

${font Arial:bold:size=10}${color Tan1}HDD ${color DarkSlateGray}${hr 2}
$font${color DimGray}/home $alignc ${fs_used /home} / ${fs_size /home} $alignr ${fs_free_perc /home}%
${fs_bar /home}
/disk $alignc ${fs_used /media/disk} / ${fs_size /media/disk} $alignr ${fs_free_perc /media/disk}%
${fs_bar /media/disk}
/disk-1 $alignc ${fs_used /media/disk-1} / ${fs_size /media/disk-1} $alignr ${fs_free_perc /media/disk-1}%
${fs_bar /media/disk-1}

${font Arial:bold:size=10}${color Tan1}TOP PROCESSES ${color DarkSlateGray}${hr 2}
${color DimGray}$font${top_mem name 2}${alignr}${top mem 2} %
$font${top_mem name 3}${alignr}${top mem 3} %
$font${top_mem name 4}${alignr}${top mem 4} %
$font${top_mem name 5}${alignr}${top mem 5} %

${font Arial:bold:size=10}${color Tan2}NETWORK ${color DarkSlateGray}${hr 2}
$font${color DimGray}IP on eth0 $alignr ${addr eth0}

Down $alignr ${downspeed eth0} kb/s
Up $alignr ${upspeed eth0} kb/s

Downloaded: $alignr  ${totaldown eth0} 
Uploaded: $alignr  ${totalup eth0}

${font Arial:bold:size=10}${color Tan2}WEATHER ${color DarkSlateGray}${hr 2}
${font}${color DimGray}

${voffset -25}${font Weather:size=45}${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=BEXX0008 --datatype=WF}
${alignc 22}${voffset -60}${font Arial:bold:size=10}${color DimGray}${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=BEXX0008 --datatype=HT}
$font${voffset -55}${alignr}${color DimGray}Wind: ${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=BEXX0008 --datatype=WS}
${alignr}${color DimGray}Humidity: ${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=BEXX0008 --datatype=HM}
${alignr}${color DimGray}Precipitation: ${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=BEXX0008 --datatype=PC}


${color DimGray}Sunrise: $alignr${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=BEXX0008 --datatype=SR}${alignr}
Sunset: $alignr${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=BEXX0008 --datatype=SS}$color

${font Arial:bold:size=10}${color Tan2}MUSIC ${color DarkSlateGray}${hr 2}
${if_running mpd}
$mpd_smart
$mpd_album
Bitrate $mpd_bitrate kbits/s
$mpd_status $mpd_elapsed/$mpd_length

${font Arial:bold:size=10}${color Tan2}TIME ${color DarkSlateGray}${hr 2}


${color DarkSlateGray} ${font :size=30}$alignc${time %H:%Mh}
${voffset -30}${font :bold:size=10}$alignc${time %d %b. %Y}
${font :bold:size=8}$alignc${time %A}
$endif


The gtk theme and fluxbox style is mire_v2

The wallpaper comes from deviantart

The icons are oxygen_refit2_white (or something like that).

---

### Post by klange on 2008-08-21
> **Opeth115 said:**
> Is that pidgin with adium theme support? if so when did this happen...?

There's an alternate branch that uses WebKit for rendering instead of a GTK text view widget. Along with it comes Adium theme support. Supposedly, it's going to end up being merged with the base code. No idea when.

### Post by aaaantoine on 2008-08-22
> **raul_ said:**
> Maybe you're missing an option because I clearly remember working with minimized windows.

But was that Compiz or Beryl?

From what I've read, Beryl had some sort of hack to retain the last known output of a minimized window.  Native support for this feature is apparently missing from Xorg, and the Compiz team would rather hold their breath and wait for said support before writing a hack.

See thread: [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=481038](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=481038)

### Post by aristotlewilde on 2008-08-24
> **masterlotep said:**
> Tintrc.?

#---------------------------------------------
# TINT CONFIG FILE
#---------------------------------------------

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL
#---------------------------------------------
panel_mode = multi_monitor
panel_monitor = 1
panel_position = bottom center
panel_size = 1920 31
panel_margin = 0 0
panel_padding = 9 3
font_shadow = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
panel_rounded = 2
panel_border_width = 2
panel_background_color = #000000 60
panel_border_color = #ff1493 66

#---------------------------------------------
# TASKS
#---------------------------------------------
task_text_centered = 1
task_width = 125
task_margin = 4
task_padding = 3
task_icon_size = 14
task_font = Shado Bold italic 9
task_font_color = #ffffff 70
task_active_font_color = #ffffff 85

#---------------------------------------------
# TASK BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
task_rounded = 2
task_background_color = #ffffff 22
task_active_background_color = #ffffff 50
task_border_width = 0
task_border_color = #ffffff 18
task_active_border_color = #ffffff 70

#---------------------------------------------
# CLOCK
#---------------------------------------------
time1_format = %A %B %d      %H:%M
time1_font = Shado Bold 10
#time2_format = %A %d %B
#time2_font = sans 8
clock_font_color = #ffffff 76

#---------------------------------------------
# MOUSE ACTION ON TASK
#---------------------------------------------
mouse_middle = none
mouse_right = close
mouse_scroll_up = toggle
mouse_scroll_down = iconify

---

### Post by iamcims on 2008-08-25
> **el mariachi said:**
> and there are a couple of native lightweight/feature full clients around:
Deluge
Transmission
KTorrent
Azureus
rTorrent
FrostWire has support for torrents
and many more

true but what do you have against utorrent, it installs and runs fine. I have used it for years. I made the switch to transmission but my utorrent connects to seeders quicker and for some reason even on the same port tends to be much faster on download speeds. I say use whatever you like, utorrent runs fine with zero errors, its very speedy also, partly due to its small size.

### Post by -grubby on 2008-08-25
> **myusername said:**
> can somebody tell me how to rum openbox with xfce so openbox is my wm? i had it for a while and then it went crazy so i cant get it completely runnig good

Just killall xfwm4 then run openbox : 

```
killall xfwm4 && sleep 2 && openbox
```

### Post by eightmillion on 2008-08-26
> **ya-manickill said:**
> I love this desktop. Its re-ignited my thoughts about KDE. Where you get the theme from?

     Thanks. You should give KDE 4.1 a shot. It's really shaping up and pretty slick. 

     My theme is really a hodge podge. The widget theme is glassified and the little computer icon in the corner is lancelot menu with a custom icon. Most of the widgets are compiled from source, but I have built packages of them and can share them if you'd like. ( In fact I've built packages of just about every plasmoid I've come across. So anyone that reads this and is looking for some particular plasmoid in deb format, message me. Chances are I have it. ) The KDE color scheme is Obsidian Dark Green. The fonts are mostly electron with hani here and there. The emerald them is a slightly modified Kore Minimal from the [Kore Suite.]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Kore+Suite?content=54701%20") The cube caps are just a solid green color. I've completely gotten rid of the KDE panel. The fact that you can't hide or even allow windows to cover it makes it supremely annoying. I just have my kmenu on my desktop along with my system tray. Instead of a taskbar, I'm using cairo dock with a bunch of custom icons. I've attached a picture of that along with my wallpaper and skydome. Hope this helps. :)

---

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-08-26
> **71CH said:**
> I know this is really OT but I just started using Tint on xubuntu and was wondering all you geniuses on this thread can help.  Can somebody please teach me how to change the time from 24-hour to 12-hour?

How about replacing %H with %I on the time section of your tintrc?

[http://tutorials.programmingsite.co.uk/cstrftime.php](http://tutorials.programmingsite.co.uk/cstrftime.php)

### Post by 71CH on 2008-08-27
This is again really really OT but can somebody explain to me why you can use compiz-fusion in xfce but not in openbox?  Aren't they kinda similar?

---

### Post by RiceMonster on 2008-08-27
> **71CH said:**
> This is again really really OT but can somebody explain to me why you can use compiz-fusion in xfce but not in openbox?  Aren't they kinda similar?

Because compiz fusion is a window manager, and so is openbox. In xfce, you're replacing xfwm4 with compiz fusion. In openbox, you'd be replacing openbox and it wouldn't be openbox anymore.

---

Well, if you see it in that light... yes, than its not simple and tidy. 3 panels... personally speaking in my setup these 3 panels are not too messy at all. By saying simple and tidy, I was referring to; for example: no icons on the desktop, no crazy funky window borders, no messy wallpaper, no fancy screenlets/conky and whatever.

### Post by SomeGuyDude on 2008-08-28
> **rossjman1 said:**
> What window decorations and icons are you using? Also where did you find that wallpaper? lol... I love your desktop!

That's shiki-colors for the GTK theme, and gnome-colors for the icons. Both are, I believe, the highest rated GTK and icons themes on gnome-look right now (BOY am I original lol). I used the "brave" version of each, that's the blue.

Wallpaper: [http://s3vendays.deviantart.com/art/Do-you-see-what-I-see-70133331](http://s3vendays.deviantart.com/art/Do-you-see-what-I-see-70133331)  It's 1280x1024 so I had to snip it some. It just so happened to fit perfectly with my conky setup, so good work there. :guitar:

The fonts are either UnDotum or Zekton, depending on which you're looking at. The more techno/robot type font is Zekton, the rounded and soft one is UnDotum.

### Post by RiceMonster on 2008-08-28
> **jimi_hendrix said:**
> is fluxbox easy to use/install because it looks nice

Well I think it's easy, but compared to GNOME, KDE, etc, it may seem difficult. If you don't want to edit configuration files, it's not for you. I say it's well worth a try though. It's easy to install and remove. You may be interested in Openbox as well, if you like Fluxbox.

### Post by klange on 2008-08-29
@What is in a name?:
You appear to be using hilight_ratio with Murrine, which is deprecated. You want "highlight_ratio" (and you also want to change the value a bit, but I don't remember in what direction, as it has either more or less of an effect than hilight_ratio)

---

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-08-29
> **WindowsSucks said:**
> @What is in a name?:
You appear to be using hilight_ratio with Murrine, which is deprecated. You want "highlight_ratio" (and you also want to change the value a bit, but I don't remember in what direction, as it has either more or less of an effect than hilight_ratio)

As I already explained at the theme's page, I'm not using the SVN version of the Murrine engine yet, to make it easier for **some** potential users who can't read the description of the theme and would complain that it looks like Windows 95 or that I broke the theme (because obviously they won't download the SVN version even if I tell them it's necessary; believe me, it happened to me with the Glow suite and the Aurora engine). I would definitely prefer to use the SVN version of Murrine, because the current one is very limited comparing to the awesome work Cimitan has been doing with the engine, though.

This leads me to a question: if I type "highlight_ratio" on the code, will the theme be compatible with the current stable version of Murrine most people use? Also, I had tried to google what the new, updated option would be, while developing ClearGlow and never found anything until you, fortunately, mentioned that to me. Thanks for that.

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-08-29
Ok, so after all I had to check this out for myself.

The "highlight_ratio" option is not compatible with the current and stable release of the Murrine engine.

Therefore, I'll have to continue to use "hilight_ratio" on my themes even though it's deprecated in the recent versions (which still accept and read that option anyway).

Besides the dark menubar and the colored menu items that Shiki-Colors also started presenting today, how similar are both themes, in the end?

I hear you on what you said about the theme being more compact. Are the buttons too large? Or is it the tabs? I tried to find a balance, in order to make the theme pleasant and not too cluttered (which can happen when you join lots of stuff in a small space). I also decided not to make the toolbars flat, since they are another different detail in ClearGlow, but is that an issue to you as a user (even though I guess that flat toolbars have the exact same size of those with a gradient)? 

I'd like to hear people further on these subjects.

---

### Post by SomeGuyDude on 2008-08-30
Same menubar, same tabs, the Metacity themes are very close, both have that idea of a colored band at the top, the buttons aren't TOO different. Some minor shape differences and ClearGlow's menu bar is a little fatter. A few other minor differences, but switching between the two almost feels like they're slight mods of the same core idea.

I don't know which came first, so I'm not accusing anyone of copying the other.

---

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-08-30
> **SomeGuyDude said:**
> Same menubar, same tabs, the Metacity themes are very close, both have that idea of a colored band at the top, the buttons aren't TOO different. Some minor shape differences and ClearGlow's menu bar is a little fatter. A few other minor differences, but switching between the two almost feels like they're slight mods of the same core idea.

I don't know which came first, so I'm not accusing anyone of copying the other.

The tabs do not look the same. They just use the same engine in both themes: Clearlooks. Look at them with a bit more attention.

In addition, there are differences in the following aspects:

- progressbars;
- sliders;
- panels;
- window background colors, both on the controls and on the text entries;
- foreground colors which were tested for hours and changed back and forth until the current result;
- scrollbars;
- toolbars;
- buttons;
- menu items (before Shiki-Colors adopted the same solution, at least);
- no bugs in Evolution's preferences dialog;
- virtually no bugs in Xfce, except for one of the applets, at least so far.

From ClearGlow's description, you could read what the inspirations for theme were. I told myself I could improve some ideas already existent in other themes and add some other details which for some people with a more demanding taste **could** indeed make all the difference. Or maybe not.

From the two themes, Shiki-Colors is the oldest one.

I do not believe that using previously tested ideas is a form of copy. Otherwise, all artists since the Renaissance would have been guilty of plagiarism.

Microsoft probably would be doomed from the start.
For other reasons, Ubuntu also wouldn't exist, by the way.

I think the concept of open source is good to allow the whole community to intervene and work in as many projects as they can and wish to. Sometimes a forked idea gives birth to something better than the original.

Some people have been redistributing some of my artwork under different names without consulting me first. I never complained about that. I also started getting a bit fed up, at some point, with all the many Elegant Brit ports that started appearing like mushrooms in some websites (basically because I needed to look at something new, which is why I kept making other stuff). I guess Lyrae could have complained about it, because Elegant Brit, Elegant One (in which I based myself first) and other works before me were based on the Black and White theme. Curiously, after developing Elegant Brit, some of the bug testing I and others made became helpful for other themes, including the original code it derived from. It's a part of what working in open source is all about. Giving and receiving. And as long as the community gets benefited from it, I'll be glad.

Many details of the artwork I produced were created in collaboration with some faithful and helpful friendsSome people have been redistributing some of my artwork under different names without consulting me first. I never complained about that. I also started getting a bit overwhelmed, at some point, with all the many Elegant Brit ports that started appearing like mushrooms in some websites (basically because I needed to look at something new to refresh my eyes, which is why I moved on and started making other stuff). I guess Lyrae could have complained about it, because in the end, that and other works before me were based on the Black and White theme. Curiously, after developing  It's a part of what working in open source is all about. And as long as the community gets benefited from it, I'll be glad. around the Web, to whom I'm thankful. Especially in the coding part, which is still my biggest weakness (I'm quite comfortable with designing the general concept, creating a vision, looking at the bigger picture, but sometimes the technical execution still puzzle me). There has also been some artistic input, and I like the way those cooperation networks appear.

ClearGlow, on the other hand, is an attempt to do something better than what already existed before. If it's not good for anything else, at least it's something I find a little bit more pleasant to have on my desktop right now than other works I have found.

If Perfectska04 feels ClearGlow (and perhaps Archiplex?) is disrespectful to his work, then I will remove my theme from openDesktop.org. Well, if that many people feel ClearGlow is not new at all, I might do that too. Meanwhile, I'd like to focus on what people find that could be improved in the theme and see what can be done with it.

---
